<p>The <b>Bahá'í Faith</b> (<a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian</a>: <span lang="fa" dir="rtl" xml:lang="fa"><span class="Nastaliq" title="Persian Nastaliq" style="font-size: 125%; font-family: 'IranNastaliq', 'Urdu Emad Nastaleeq', 'Noto Nastaliq Urdu', 'Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft', 'Urdu Typesetting', 'Jameel Noori Nastaleeq', 'Hussaini Nastaleeq', 'AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq', 'Nafees Nastaleeq', 'Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01', Nafees, 'Pak Nastaleeq', 'PDMS_Jauhar', 'Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq';">بهائیت</span></span>‎‎ <i>Bahá'iyyat</i>, <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language" class="mw-redirect">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl" xml:lang="ar"><span class="script-arabic script-Arab" dir="rtl" style="font-family:Scheherazade,Lateef,Arial,'Arabic Transparent','Droid Arabic Naskh',Amiri,'Microsoft Sans Serif','Segoe UI','Sakkal Majalla','Microsoft Uighur','Arabic Typesetting',sans-serif,serif;font-weight:normal;">بهائية</span>‎</span>‎ <i>Bahá'iyya</i> <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/ə/ 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'h' in 'hi'">h</span><span title="/aɪ/ long 'i' in 'tide'">aɪ</span></span>/</a></span></span><sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1"><span>[</span>note 1<span>]</span></a></sup>) is a <a href="/wiki/Monotheism" title="Monotheism">monotheistic</a> religion which emphasizes the spiritual unity of all <a href="/wiki/Humankind" title="Humankind" class="mw-redirect">humankind</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDictionary2004_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDictionary2004-2"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> Three core principles establish a basis for Bahá'í teachings and doctrine: the <a href="/wiki/God_in_the_Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith" title="God in the Bahá'í Faith">unity of God</a>, that there is only one <a href="/wiki/God" title="God">God</a> who is the source of all <a href="/wiki/Creation_myth" title="Creation myth">creation</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith_and_the_unity_of_religion" title="Bahá'í Faith and the unity of religion">unity of religion</a>, that all major religions have the same spiritual source and come from the same God; and the <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith_and_the_unity_of_humanity" title="Bahá'í Faith and the unity of humanity">unity of humanity</a>, that all humans have been created equal, coupled with the <a href="/wiki/Unity_in_diversity" title="Unity in diversity">unity in diversity</a>, that diversity of race and culture are seen as worthy of appreciation and acceptance.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHutter2005737.E2.80.93740_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHutter2005737.E2.80.93740-3"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> According to the Bahá'í Faith's teachings, the human purpose is to learn to know and to love God through such methods as <a href="/wiki/Prayer_in_the_Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith" title="Prayer in the Bahá'í Faith">prayer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Introspection" title="Introspection">reflection</a> and being of service to humanity.</p>
<p>The Bahá'í Faith was founded by <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27u%27ll%C3%A1h" title="Bahá'u'lláh">Bahá'u'lláh</a> in 19th-century <a href="/wiki/Persia" title="Persia" class="mw-redirect">Persia</a>. Bahá'u'lláh was exiled for his teachings from Persia to the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> and died while officially still a prisoner. After Bahá'u'lláh's death, under the leadership of his son, <a href="/wiki/%60Abdu%27l-Bah%C3%A1" title="`Abdu'l-Bahá">`Abdu'l-Bahá</a>, the religion spread from its Persian and Ottoman roots, and gained a footing in Europe and America, and was consolidated in Iran, where it suffers intense <a href="/wiki/Persecution_of_Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%ADs" title="Persecution of Bahá'ís">persecution</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAffolterJanuary_200575.E2.80.93114_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAffolterJanuary_200575.E2.80.93114-4"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> After the death of `Abdu'l-Bahá, the leadership of the Bahá'í community entered a new phase, evolving from a single individual to an administrative order with both elected bodies and appointed individuals.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith200856_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith200856-5"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> There are probably more than 5 million Bahá'ís around the world in more than 200 countries and territories.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHutter2005737.E2.80.9340_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHutter2005737.E2.80.9340-6"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>note 2<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In the Bahá'í Faith, religious history is seen to have unfolded through a series of divine messengers, each of whom established a religion that was suited to the needs of the time and to the capacity of the people. These messengers have included <a href="/wiki/Abrahamic" title="Abrahamic" class="mw-redirect">Abrahamic</a> figures—<a href="/wiki/Moses" title="Moses">Moses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jesus" title="Jesus">Jesus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Muhammad" title="Muhammad">Muhammad</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Indian_religions" title="Indian religions">Indian</a> ones—<a href="/wiki/Krishna" title="Krishna">Krishna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buddha" title="Buddha" class="mw-redirect">Buddha</a>, and others. For Bahá'ís, the most recent messengers are the <a href="/wiki/B%C3%A1b" title="Báb">Báb</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27u%27ll%C3%A1h" title="Bahá'u'lláh">Bahá'u'lláh</a>. In Bahá'í belief, each consecutive messenger prophesied of messengers to follow, and Bahá'u'lláh's life and teachings fulfilled the <a href="/wiki/Eschatology" title="Eschatology">end-time</a> promises of previous scriptures. Humanity is understood to be in a process of collective evolution, and the need of the present time is for the gradual establishment of peace, justice and unity on a global scale.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2008107.E2.80.939_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2008107.E2.80.939-8"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The word <i>Bahá'í </i> is used either as an adjective to refer to the Bahá'í Faith or as a term for a follower of Bahá'u'lláh. The word is not a noun meaning the religion as a whole.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStockman2006_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStockman2006-9"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> It is derived from the Arabic <i><a href="/wiki/Greatest_Name" title="Greatest Name" class="mw-redirect">Bahá' </a></i> (<span lang="ar" xml:lang="ar">بهاء</span>), meaning "glory" or "splendor".<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>note 3<span>]</span></a></sup> The term "Bahaism" (or "Baha'ism") is still used, mainly in a pejorative sense.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHatcherMartin1998xiii_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHatcherMartin1998xiii-11"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECentre_for_Faith_and_the_Media_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECentre_for_Faith_and_the_Media-12"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Beliefs">Beliefs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Beliefs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Three core principles establish a basis for Bahá'í teachings and doctrine: the <a href="/wiki/God_in_the_Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith" title="God in the Bahá'í Faith">unity of God</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith_and_the_unity_of_religion" title="Bahá'í Faith and the unity of religion">unity of religion</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith_and_the_unity_of_humanity" title="Bahá'í Faith and the unity of humanity">unity of humanity</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHutter2005737.E2.80.93740_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHutter2005737.E2.80.93740-3"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> From these postulates stems the belief that God periodically reveals his will through divine messengers, whose purpose is to transform the character of humankind and to develop, within those who respond, moral and spiritual qualities. Religion is thus seen as orderly, unified, and progressive from age to age.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2008108.E2.80.93109_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2008108.E2.80.93109-13"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="God">God</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: God">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/God_in_the_Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith" title="God in the Bahá'í Faith">God in the Bahá'í Faith</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bahaitemplesydney.JPG" class="image"><img alt="A white domed building" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Bahaitemplesydney.JPG/170px-Bahaitemplesydney.JPG" width="170" height="229" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Bahaitemplesydney.JPG/255px-Bahaitemplesydney.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Bahaitemplesydney.JPG/340px-Bahaitemplesydney.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1662" data-file-height="2243" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bahaitemplesydney.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bahá'í Temple, <a href="/wiki/Ingleside,_New_South_Wales" title="Ingleside, New South Wales">Ingleside</a>, Sydney, Australia</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Bahá'í writings describe a single, personal, inaccessible, omniscient, omnipresent, imperishable, and almighty God who is the creator of all things in the universe.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2008106_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2008106-14"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Existence_of_God" title="Existence of God">existence of God</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Universe" title="Universe">universe</a> is thought to be eternal, without a beginning or end.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBritannica1992_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBritannica1992-15"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> Though inaccessible directly, God is nevertheless seen as conscious of creation, with a will and purpose that is expressed through messengers termed <a href="/wiki/Manifestations_of_God" title="Manifestations of God" class="mw-redirect">Manifestations of God</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2008106.E2.80.93107_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2008106.E2.80.93107-16"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2008111.E2.80.93112_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2008111.E2.80.93112-17"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Bahá'í teachings state that God is too great for humans to fully comprehend, or to create a complete and accurate image of, by themselves. Therefore, human understanding of God is achieved through his revelations via his Manifestations.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHatcher20051.E2.80.9338_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHatcher20051.E2.80.9338-18"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECole19821.E2.80.9338_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECole19821.E2.80.9338-19"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> In the Bahá'í religion, God is often referred to by titles and attributes (for example, the All-Powerful, or the All-Loving), and there is a substantial emphasis on <a href="/wiki/Monotheism" title="Monotheism">monotheism</a>; such doctrines as the <a href="/wiki/Trinity" title="Trinity">Trinity</a> are seen as compromising, if not contradicting, the Bahá'í view that God is single and has no equal.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStockman1992_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStockman1992-20"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> The Bahá'í teachings state that the attributes which are applied to God are used to translate Godliness into human terms and also to help individuals concentrate on their own attributes in worshipping God to develop their potentialities on their spiritual path.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHatcher20051-38_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHatcher20051-38-21"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECole19821-38_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECole19821-38-22"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> According to the Bahá'í teachings the human purpose is to learn to know and love God through such methods as <a href="/wiki/Prayer_in_the_Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith" title="Prayer in the Bahá'í Faith">prayer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Introspection" title="Introspection">reflection</a>, and being of service to others.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHatcher20051-38_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHatcher20051-38-21"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wilmette_how_side.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A white column with ornate designs carved into it, including a Star of David" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Wilmette_how_side.jpg/170px-Wilmette_how_side.jpg" width="170" height="232" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Wilmette_how_side.jpg/255px-Wilmette_how_side.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Wilmette_how_side.jpg/340px-Wilmette_how_side.jpg 2x" data-file-width="967" data-file-height="1317" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wilmette_how_side.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Symbols of many religions on a pillar of the <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_House_of_Worship_(Wilmette,_Illinois)" title="Bahá'í House of Worship (Wilmette, Illinois)">Bahá'í House of Worship</a> in Wilmette, Illinois, U.S.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith_and_the_unity_of_religion" title="Bahá'í Faith and the unity of religion">Bahá'í Faith and the unity of religion</a></div>
<div class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Progressive_revelation_(Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD)" title="Progressive revelation (Bahá'í)">Progressive revelation (Bahá'í)</a></div>
<p>Bahá'í notions of progressive religious revelation result in their accepting the validity of the well known religions of the world, whose founders and central figures are seen as Manifestations of God. Religious history is interpreted as a series of <a href="/wiki/Dispensationalism" title="Dispensationalism">dispensations</a>, where each <i>manifestation</i> brings a somewhat broader and more advanced <a href="/wiki/Revelation" title="Revelation">revelation</a> that is rendered as a text of scripture and passed on through history with greater or lesser reliability but at least true in substance,<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> suited for the time and place in which it was expressed.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDaumeWatson1992_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDaumeWatson1992-24"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> Specific religious social teachings (for example, the direction of prayer, or dietary restrictions) may be revoked by a subsequent manifestation so that a more appropriate requirement for the time and place may be established. Conversely, certain general principles (for example, neighbourliness, or charity) are seen to be universal and consistent. In Bahá'í belief, this process of progressive revelation will not end; however, it is believed to be cyclical. Bahá'ís do not expect a new manifestation of God to appear within 1000 years of Bahá'u'lláh's revelation.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcMullen20007_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcMullen20007-25"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Bahá'í beliefs are sometimes described as <a href="/wiki/Syncretism" title="Syncretism">syncretic</a> combinations of earlier religious beliefs.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStockman1997_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStockman1997-26"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> Bahá'ís, however, assert that their religion is a distinct tradition with its own <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_literature" title="Bahá'í literature">scriptures</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_teachings" title="Bahá'í teachings">teachings</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_laws" title="Bahá'í laws">laws</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_history" title="Bahá'í history" class="mw-redirect">history</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDaumeWatson1992_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDaumeWatson1992-24"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBausani2012_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBausani2012-27"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> While the religion was initially seen as a sect of Islam, most religious specialists now see it as an independent religion, with its religious background in <a href="/wiki/Shi%27a_Islam" title="Shi'a Islam" class="mw-redirect">Shi'a Islam</a> being seen as analogous to the Jewish context in which Christianity was established.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVan_der_Vyer1996449_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVan_der_Vyer1996449-28"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> Muslim institutions and clergy, both <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">Sunni</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shia_Islam" title="Shia Islam">Shia</a>, consider Bahá'ís to be deserters or <a href="/wiki/Apostasy_in_Islam" title="Apostasy in Islam">apostates from Islam</a>, which has led to Bahá'ís being <a href="/wiki/Persecution_of_Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%ADs" title="Persecution of Bahá'ís">persecuted</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBoyleSheen1997119-120_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoyleSheen1997119-120-29"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAfshari2001119-120_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAfshari2001119-120-30"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> Bahá'ís describe their faith as an independent world religion, differing from the other traditions in its relative age and in the appropriateness of Bahá'u'lláh's teachings to the modern context.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELundberg2005_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELundberg2005-31"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> Bahá'u'lláh is believed to have fulfilled the <a href="/wiki/Eschatology" title="Eschatology">messianic expectations</a> of these precursor faiths.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBuck2004143-178_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBuck2004143-178-32"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_beings">Human beings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Human beings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ringstone.svg" class="image"><img alt="A stylized Arabic figure which has intersecting lines that lock around rings and five-pointed stars to either side" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Ringstone.svg/220px-Ringstone.svg.png" width="220" height="113" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Ringstone.svg/330px-Ringstone.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Ringstone.svg/440px-Ringstone.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1052" data-file-height="540" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ringstone.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_symbols#Ringstone_symbol" title="Bahá'í symbols">Ringstone symbol</a> represents humanity's connection to God</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith_and_the_unity_of_humanity" title="Bahá'í Faith and the unity of humanity">Bahá'í Faith and the unity of humanity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith_on_life_after_death" title="Bahá'í Faith on life after death">Bahá'í Faith on life after death</a></div>
<p>The Bahá'í writings state that human beings have a "rational <a href="/wiki/Soul_(spirit)" title="Soul (spirit)" class="mw-redirect">soul</a>", and that this provides the species with a unique capacity to recognize God's station and humanity's relationship with its creator. Every human is seen to have a duty to recognize God through His <a href="/wiki/Manifestation_of_God" title="Manifestation of God">messengers</a>, and to conform to their teachings.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcMullen200057-58_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcMullen200057-58-33"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> Through recognition and obedience, service to humanity and regular prayer and spiritual practice, the Bahá'í writings state that the soul becomes closer to God, the spiritual ideal in Bahá'í belief. When a human dies, the soul passes into the next world, where its spiritual development in the physical world becomes a basis for judgment and advancement in the spiritual world. Heaven and Hell are taught to be spiritual states of nearness or distance from God that describe relationships in this world and the next, and not physical places of reward and punishment achieved after death.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasumian1995_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasumian1995-34"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The Bahá'í writings emphasize the essential equality of human beings, and the abolition of prejudice. Humanity is seen as essentially one, though highly varied; its diversity of race and culture are seen as worthy of appreciation and acceptance. Doctrines of racism, nationalism, caste, social class, and gender-based hierarchy are seen as artificial impediments to unity.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHutter2005737.E2.80.93740_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHutter2005737.E2.80.93740-3"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> The Bahá'í teachings state that the unification of humanity is the paramount issue in the religious and political conditions of the present world.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDaumeWatson1992_24-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDaumeWatson1992-24"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Teachings">Teachings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Teachings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="vertical-navbox nowraplinks plainlist" style="float:right;clear:right;width:22.0em;margin:0 0 1.0em 1.0em;background:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;padding:0.2em;border-spacing:0.4em 0;text-align:center;line-height:1.4em;font-size:88%;width:auto;border:1px solid #060;">

<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_teachings" title="Bahá'í teachings">Bahá'í teachings</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Summary">Summary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Summary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Shoghi_Effendi" title="Shoghi Effendi">Shoghi Effendi</a>, the appointed head of the religion from 1921 to 1957, wrote the following summary of what he considered to be the distinguishing principles of <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27u%27ll%C3%A1h" title="Bahá'u'lláh">Bahá'u'lláh</a>'s teachings, which, he said, together with the laws and ordinances of the <i><a href="/wiki/Kit%C3%A1b-i-Aqdas" title="Kitáb-i-Aqdas">Kitáb-i-Aqdas</a></i> constitute the bedrock of the Bahá'í Faith:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>The independent search after truth, unfettered by <a href="/wiki/Superstition" title="Superstition">superstition</a> or tradition; the oneness of the entire <a href="/wiki/Human" title="Human">human race</a>, the pivotal principle and fundamental doctrine of the Faith; the basic unity of all religions; the condemnation of all forms of <a href="/wiki/Prejudice" title="Prejudice">prejudice</a>, whether religious, racial, class or national; the harmony which must exist between religion and science; the equality of men and women, the two wings on which the bird of human kind is able to soar; the introduction of compulsory education; the adoption of a <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith_and_auxiliary_language" title="Bahá'í Faith and auxiliary language">universal auxiliary language</a>; the abolition of the extremes of wealth and poverty; the institution of a <a href="/wiki/World_government" title="World government">world tribunal</a> for the adjudication of disputes between nations; the exaltation of work, performed in the spirit of service, to the rank of <a href="/wiki/Worship" title="Worship">worship</a>; the glorification of justice as the ruling principle in human society, and of religion as a bulwark for the protection of all peoples and nations; and the establishment of a permanent and <a href="/wiki/World_peace" title="World peace">universal peace</a> as the supreme goal of all mankind—these stand out as the essential elements [which Bahá'u'lláh proclaimed].<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEffendi1944281-282_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEffendi1944281-282-35"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_principles">Social principles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Social principles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The following principles are frequently listed as a quick summary of the Bahá'í teachings. They are derived from transcripts of speeches given by <a href="/wiki/%60Abdu%27l-Bah%C3%A1" title="`Abdu'l-Bahá">`Abdu'l-Bahá</a> during his tour of Europe and North America in 1912.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith200852.E2.80.9353_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith200852.E2.80.9353-36"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrinciples_of_the_Bah.C3.A1.27.C3.AD_Faith26_March_2006_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrinciples_of_the_Bah.C3.A1.27.C3.AD_Faith26_March_2006-37"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> The list is not authoritative and a variety of such lists circulate.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBausani2012_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBausani2012-27"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECole1989438-446_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECole1989438-446-38"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/God_in_the_Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith" title="God in the Bahá'í Faith">Unity of God</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith_and_the_unity_of_religion" title="Bahá'í Faith and the unity of religion">Unity of religion</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith_and_the_unity_of_humanity" title="Bahá'í Faith and the unity of humanity">Unity of humanity</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Unity_in_diversity" title="Unity in diversity">Unity in diversity</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith_and_gender_equality" title="Bahá'í Faith and gender equality">Equality between men and women</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith_and_the_unity_of_humanity" title="Bahá'í Faith and the unity of humanity">Elimination of all forms of prejudice</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/World_peace" title="World peace">World peace</a> and a <a href="/wiki/New_world_order_(Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD)" title="New world order (Bahá'í)">New world order</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith_and_science" title="Bahá'í Faith and science">Harmony of religion and science</a></li>
<li>Independent investigation of truth</li>
<li>Principle of Ever-Advancing Civilization</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith_and_education" title="Bahá'í Faith and education">Universal compulsory education</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith_and_auxiliary_language" title="Bahá'í Faith and auxiliary language">Universal auxiliary language</a><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>note 4<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Obedience to government and non-involvement in partisan politics unless submission to law amounts to a denial of Faith.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>note 5<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Elimination of extremes of wealth and poverty</li>
</ul>
<p>With specific regard to the pursuit of <a href="/wiki/World_peace" title="World peace">world peace</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27u%27ll%C3%A1h" title="Bahá'u'lláh">Bahá'u'lláh</a> prescribed a world-embracing <a href="/wiki/Collective_security" title="Collective security">collective security</a> arrangement as necessary for the establishment of a lasting peace.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2000266-267_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2000266-267-41"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mystical_teachings">Mystical teachings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Mystical teachings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Although the <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_teachings" title="Bahá'í teachings">Bahá'í teachings</a> have a strong emphasis on social and ethical issues, there exist a number of foundational texts that have been described as mystical.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDaumeWatson1992_24-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDaumeWatson1992-24"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/Seven_Valleys" title="Seven Valleys" class="mw-redirect">Seven Valleys</a></i> is considered Bahá'u'lláh's "greatest mystical composition." It was written to a follower of <a href="/wiki/Sufism" title="Sufism">Sufism</a>, in the style of <a href="/wiki/Attar_Neyshapuri" title="Attar Neyshapuri" class="mw-redirect"><span style="white-space:nowrap;">&#160;</span>`Attar</a>, The <a href="/wiki/Persian_people" title="Persian people">Persian</a> Muslim poet,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2000311_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2000311-42"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> and sets forth the stages of the soul's journey towards God. It was first translated into English in 1906, becoming one of the earliest available books of Bahá'u'lláh to the West. The <i><a href="/wiki/Hidden_Words" title="Hidden Words">Hidden Words</a></i> is another book written by Bahá'u'lláh during the same period, containing 153 short passages in which Bahá'u'lláh claims to have taken the basic essence of certain spiritual truths and written them in brief form.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2000181_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2000181-43"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Covenant">Covenant</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Covenant">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Covenant_of_Bah%C3%A1%27u%27ll%C3%A1h" title="Covenant of Bahá'u'lláh">Covenant of Bahá'u'lláh</a></div>
<p>The Bahá'í teachings speak of both a "Greater Covenant",<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETaherzadeh1972_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETaherzadeh1972-44"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> being universal and endless, and a "Lesser Covenant", being unique to each religious dispensation. The Lesser Covenant is viewed as an agreement between a Messenger of God and his followers and includes social practices and the continuation of authority in the religion. At this time Bahá'ís view Bahá'u'lláh's revelation as a binding lesser covenant for his followers; in the Bahá'í writings being firm in the covenant is considered a virtue to work toward.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMomen1995_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMomen1995-45"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> The Greater Covenant is viewed as a more enduring agreement between God and humanity, where a Manifestation of God is expected to come to humanity about every thousand years, at times of turmoil and uncertainty. With unity as an essential teaching of the religion, Bahá'ís follow an <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_administration" title="Bahá'í administration">administration</a> they believe is divinely ordained, and therefore see attempts to create schisms and divisions as efforts that are contrary to the teachings of Bahá'u'lláh. Schisms have occurred over the succession of authority, but any <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_divisions" title="Bahá'í divisions">Bahá'í divisions</a> have had relatively little success and have failed to attract a sizeable following.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMacEoin1989448_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacEoin1989448-46"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> The followers of such divisions are regarded as <a href="/wiki/Covenant-breaker" title="Covenant-breaker">Covenant-breakers</a> and shunned, essentially <a href="/wiki/Excommunication" title="Excommunication">excommunicated</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMomen1995_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMomen1995-45"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2008173_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2008173-47"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Canonical_texts">Canonical texts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Canonical texts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_literature" title="Bahá'í literature">Bahá'í literature</a></div>
<p>The <i>canonical texts</i> are the writings of the <a href="/wiki/B%C3%A1b" title="Báb">Báb</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27u%27ll%C3%A1h" title="Bahá'u'lláh">Bahá'u'lláh</a>, <a href="/wiki/%60Abdu%27l-Bah%C3%A1" title="`Abdu'l-Bahá">`Abdu'l-Bahá</a>, Shoghi Effendi and the <a href="/wiki/Universal_House_of_Justice" title="Universal House of Justice">Universal House of Justice</a>, and the authenticated talks of `Abdu'l-Bahá. The writings of the Báb and Bahá'u'lláh are considered as divine revelation, the writings and talks of `Abdu'l-Bahá and the writings of Shoghi Effendi as authoritative interpretation, and those of the Universal House of Justice as authoritative legislation and elucidation. Some measure of divine guidance is assumed for all of these texts.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2000100-101_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2000100-101-48"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> Some of Bahá'u'lláh's most important writings include the <a href="/wiki/Kit%C3%A1b-i-Aqdas" title="Kitáb-i-Aqdas">Kitáb-i-Aqdas</a>, literally the <i>Most Holy Book</i>, which is his book of laws,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHatcherMartin199846_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHatcherMartin199846-49"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Kit%C3%A1b-i-%C3%8Dq%C3%A1n" title="Kitáb-i-Íqán">Kitáb-i-Íqán</a>, literally the <i>Book of Certitude</i>, which became the foundation of much of Bahá'í belief,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHatcherMartin1998137_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHatcherMartin1998137-50"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Gems_of_Divine_Mysteries" title="Gems of Divine Mysteries">Gems of Divine Mysteries</a>, which includes further doctrinal foundations, and the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Valleys" title="Seven Valleys" class="mw-redirect">Seven Valleys</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Four_Valleys" title="The Four Valleys">the Four Valleys</a> which are mystical treatises.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith200820_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith200820-51"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table style="float:right; width:20%; border:1px solid #ddd; margin:0 0 1em 1em; padding:0 0 1em 1em; vertical-align:right; font-size:80%;">

<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_history" title="Bahá'í history" class="mw-redirect">Bahá'í history</a></div>
<p>Bahá'í history follows a sequence of leaders, beginning with the <a href="/wiki/B%C3%A1b" title="Báb">Báb</a>'s declaration in <a href="/wiki/Shiraz,_Iran" title="Shiraz, Iran" class="mw-redirect">Shiraz, Iran</a> on the evening of 22 May 1844, and ultimately resting on an administrative order established by the central figures of the religion. The Bahá'í community was mostly confined to the <a href="/wiki/Qajar_dynasty" title="Qajar dynasty">Persian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman</a> empires until after the death of Bahá'u'lláh in 1892, at which time he had followers in 13 countries of Asia and Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETaherzadeh1987125_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETaherzadeh1987125-52"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> Under the leadership of his son, `Abdu'l-Bahá, the religion gained a footing in Europe and America, and was consolidated in Iran, where it still suffers intense <a href="/wiki/Persecution_of_Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%ADs" title="Persecution of Bahá'ís">persecution</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAffolterJanuary_200575.E2.80.93114_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAffolterJanuary_200575.E2.80.93114-4"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> After the death of `Abdu'l-Bahá in 1921, the leadership of the Bahá'í community entered a new phase, evolving from a single individual to an administrative order with both elected bodies and appointed individuals.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith200856_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith200856-5"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_B.C3.A1b">The Báb</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: The Báb">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/B%C3%A1b" title="Báb">Báb</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Shrine_Bab_North_West.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A domed building" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Shrine_Bab_North_West.jpg/170px-Shrine_Bab_North_West.jpg" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Shrine_Bab_North_West.jpg/255px-Shrine_Bab_North_West.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Shrine_Bab_North_West.jpg/340px-Shrine_Bab_North_West.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="3072" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Shrine_Bab_North_West.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Shrine_of_the_B%C3%A1b" title="Shrine of the Báb">Shrine of the Báb</a> in Haifa, Israel</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On the evening of 22 May 1844, Siyyid `Alí-Muhammad of Shiraz, Iran proclaimed that he was "the Báb" (<span lang="ar" xml:lang="ar">الباب</span> "the Gate"), referring to his later claim to the station of <a href="/wiki/Mahdi" title="Mahdi">Mahdi</a>, the Twelfth Imam of <a href="/wiki/Shi%27a_Islam" title="Shi'a Islam" class="mw-redirect">Shi`a Islam</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAffolterJanuary_200575.E2.80.93114_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAffolterJanuary_200575.E2.80.93114-4"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> His followers were therefore known as <a href="/wiki/B%C3%A1bism" title="Bábism">Bábís</a>. As the Báb's teachings spread, which the Islamic clergy saw as a threat, his followers came under increased persecution and torture.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDaumeWatson1992_24-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDaumeWatson1992-24"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> The conflicts escalated in several places to military sieges by the <a href="/wiki/List_of_kings_of_Persia" title="List of kings of Persia">Shah</a>'s army. The Báb himself was imprisoned and eventually executed in 1850.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWinter17_September_1997_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWinter17_September_1997-53"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Bahá'ís see the Báb as the forerunner of the Bahá'í Faith, because the Báb's writings introduced the concept of "<a href="/wiki/He_whom_God_shall_make_manifest" title="He whom God shall make manifest">He whom God shall make manifest</a>", a Messianic figure whose coming, according to Bahá'ís, was announced in the scriptures of all of the world's great religions, and whom Bahá'u'lláh, the founder of the Bahá'í Faith, claimed to be in 1863.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDaumeWatson1992_24-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDaumeWatson1992-24"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Shrine_of_the_B%C3%A1b" title="Shrine of the Báb">The Báb's tomb</a>, located in <a href="/wiki/Haifa" title="Haifa">Haifa, Israel</a>, is an important place of <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_pilgrimage" title="Bahá'í pilgrimage">pilgrimage</a> for Bahá'ís. The remains of the Báb were brought secretly from <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> to the Holy Land and eventually interred in the tomb built for them in a spot specifically designated by Bahá'u'lláh.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBalyuzi2001_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBalyuzi2001-54"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> The main written works translated into English of the Báb's are collected in <a href="/wiki/Selections_from_the_Writings_of_the_B%C3%A1b" title="Selections from the Writings of the Báb">Selections from the Writings of the Báb</a> out of the estimated 135 works.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUniversal_House_of_JusticeSeptember_2002349-350_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUniversal_House_of_JusticeSeptember_2002349-350-55"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bah.C3.A1.27u.27ll.C3.A1h">Bahá'u'lláh</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Bahá'u'lláh">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27u%27ll%C3%A1h" title="Bahá'u'lláh">Bahá'u'lláh</a></div>
<p>Mírzá Husayn `Alí Núrí was one of the early followers of the Báb, and later took the title of Bahá'u'lláh. He was arrested and imprisoned for this involvement in 1852. Bahá'u'lláh relates that in 1853, while incarcerated in the dungeon of the <a href="/wiki/S%C3%ADy%C3%A1h-Ch%C3%A1l" title="Síyáh-Chál">Síyáh-Chál</a> in <a href="/wiki/Tehran" title="Tehran">Tehran</a>, he received the first intimations that he was the one anticipated by the Báb.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHutter2005737.E2.80.93740_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHutter2005737.E2.80.93740-3"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Shortly thereafter he was expelled from <a href="/wiki/Tehran" title="Tehran">Tehran</a> to <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">Baghdad</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHutter2005737.E2.80.93740_3-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHutter2005737.E2.80.93740-3"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> then to Constantinople (now <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a>); and then to Adrianople (now <a href="/wiki/Edirne" title="Edirne">Edirne</a>). In 1863, at the time of his banishment from Baghdad to Constantinople, Bahá'u'lláh declared his claim to a divine mission to his family and followers. Tensions then grew between him and <a href="/wiki/Subh-i-Azal" title="Subh-i-Azal">Subh-i-Azal</a>, the appointed leader of the Bábís who did not recognize Bahá'u'lláh's claim. Throughout the rest of his life Bahá'u'lláh gained the allegiance of most of the Bábís, who came to be known as Bahá'ís. Beginning in 1866, he began declaring his mission as a Messenger of God in letters to the world's religious and secular rulers, including <a href="/wiki/Pope_Pius_IX" title="Pope Pius IX">Pope Pius IX</a>, <a href="/wiki/Napoleon_III" title="Napoleon III">Napoleon III</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Queen_Victoria" title="Queen Victoria">Queen Victoria</a>.</p>
<p>In 1868 Bahá'u'lláh was banished by Sultan <a href="/wiki/Abd%C3%BCl%C3%A2ziz" title="Abdülâziz" class="mw-redirect">Abdülâziz</a> a final time to the Ottoman penal colony of <a href="/wiki/Acre,_Israel" title="Acre, Israel">`Akká</a>, in present-day <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>. Towards the end of his life, the strict and harsh confinement was gradually relaxed, and he was allowed to live in a home near `Akká, while still officially a prisoner of that city.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECole1989422-429_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECole1989422-429-56"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> He died there in 1892. Bahá'ís regard his resting place at <a href="/wiki/Mansion_of_Bahj%C3%AD" title="Mansion of Bahjí">Bahjí</a> as the <a href="/wiki/Qiblih" title="Qiblih">Qiblih</a> to which they turn in prayer each day.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith200820.E2.80.9321.2C_28_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith200820.E2.80.9321.2C_28-57"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Bahá'u'lláh wrote <a href="/wiki/List_of_writings_of_Bah%C3%A1%27u%27ll%C3%A1h" title="List of writings of Bahá'u'lláh">many written works</a> taken as scripture in the religion of which only a fraction have been translated into English.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith200079-80_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith200079-80-58"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> There have been 15,000 works both small and large noted<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUniversal_House_of_JusticeSeptember_2002349-350_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUniversal_House_of_JusticeSeptember_2002349-350-55"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> - the most significant of which are the <a href="/wiki/Kit%C3%A1b-i-Aqdas" title="Kitáb-i-Aqdas">Most Holy Book</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Kit%C3%A1b-i-%C3%8Dq%C3%A1n" title="Kitáb-i-Íqán">Book of Certitude</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Hidden_Words" title="Hidden Words">Hidden Words</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Valleys" title="Seven Valleys" class="mw-redirect">Seven Valleys</a>. There is also a series of compilation volumes of smaller works the most significant of which is the <a href="/wiki/Gleanings_from_the_Writings_of_Bah%C3%A1%27u%27ll%C3%A1h" title="Gleanings from the Writings of Bahá'u'lláh">Gleanings from the Writings of Bahá'u'lláh</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id=".60Abdu.27l-Bah.C3.A1">`Abdu'l-Bahá</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: `Abdu'l-Bahá">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%E2%80%98Abdu%E2%80%99l-Bah%C3%A1_portrait.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/%E2%80%98Abdu%E2%80%99l-Bah%C3%A1_portrait.jpg/220px-%E2%80%98Abdu%E2%80%99l-Bah%C3%A1_portrait.jpg" width="220" height="272" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/%E2%80%98Abdu%E2%80%99l-Bah%C3%A1_portrait.jpg/330px-%E2%80%98Abdu%E2%80%99l-Bah%C3%A1_portrait.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/%E2%80%98Abdu%E2%80%99l-Bah%C3%A1_portrait.jpg/440px-%E2%80%98Abdu%E2%80%99l-Bah%C3%A1_portrait.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2864" data-file-height="3543" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%E2%80%98Abdu%E2%80%99l-Bah%C3%A1_portrait.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
`Abdu'l-Bahá</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/%60Abdu%27l-Bah%C3%A1" title="`Abdu'l-Bahá">`Abdu'l-Bahá</a></div>
<p>`Abbás Effendi was Bahá'u'lláh's eldest son, known by the title of `Abdu'l-Bahá (Servant of Bahá). His father left a <a href="/wiki/Tablets_of_Bah%C3%A1%27u%27ll%C3%A1h#Kit.C3.A1b-i-.60Ahd_.28Book_of_the_Covenant.29" title="Tablets of Bahá'u'lláh" class="mw-redirect">Will</a> that appointed `Abdu'l-Bahá as the leader of the Bahá'í community, and designated him as the "Centre of the Covenant", "Head of the Faith", and the sole authoritative interpreter of Bahá'u'lláh's writings.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBalyuzi2001_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBalyuzi2001-54"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith200847_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith200847-59"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> `Abdu'l-Bahá had shared his father's long exile and imprisonment, which continued until `Abdu'l-Bahá's own release as a result of the <a href="/wiki/Young_Turk_Revolution" title="Young Turk Revolution">Young Turk Revolution</a> in 1908. Following his release he led a life of travelling, speaking, teaching, and maintaining correspondence with communities of believers and individuals, expounding the principles of the Bahá'í Faith.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHutter2005737.E2.80.93740_3-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHutter2005737.E2.80.93740-3"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>It is estimated that `Abdu'l-Bahá wrote over 27,000 works mostly in the form of letters of which only a fraction have been translated into English.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUniversal_House_of_JusticeSeptember_2002349-350_55-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUniversal_House_of_JusticeSeptember_2002349-350-55"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> Among the more well known are <i><a href="/wiki/The_Secret_of_Divine_Civilization" title="The Secret of Divine Civilization">The Secret of Divine Civilization</a></i>, the <i><a href="/wiki/Tablet_to_Dr._Forel" title="Tablet to Dr. Forel">Tablet to Auguste-Henri Forel</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Some_Answered_Questions" title="Some Answered Questions">Some Answered Questions</a></i>. Additionally notes taken of a number of his talks were published in various volumes like <i><a href="/wiki/Paris_Talks" title="Paris Talks">Paris Talks</a></i> during his <a href="/wiki/%60Abdu%27l-Bah%C3%A1%27s_journeys_to_the_West" title="`Abdu'l-Bahá's journeys to the West">journeys to the West</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bah.C3.A1.27.C3.AD_administration">Bahá'í administration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Bahá'í administration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_administration" title="Bahá'í administration">Bahá'í administration</a></div>
<p>Bahá'u'lláh's <i><a href="/wiki/Kit%C3%A1b-i-Aqdas" title="Kitáb-i-Aqdas">Kitáb-i-Aqdas</a></i> and <i>The <a href="/wiki/Will_and_Testament_of_%60Abdu%27l-Bah%C3%A1" title="Will and Testament of `Abdu'l-Bahá">Will and Testament of `Abdu'l-Bahá</a></i> are foundational documents of the Bahá'í administrative order. Bahá'u'lláh established the elected <a href="/wiki/Universal_House_of_Justice" title="Universal House of Justice">Universal House of Justice</a>, and `Abdu'l-Bahá established the appointed hereditary Guardianship and clarified the relationship between the two institutions.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBalyuzi2001_54-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBalyuzi2001-54"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith200855.E2.80.9357_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith200855.E2.80.9357-60"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> In his Will, `Abdu'l-Bahá appointed his eldest grandson, Shoghi Effendi, as the first <i>Guardian</i> of the Bahá'í Faith, serving as head of the religion until his death, for 36 years.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith200855_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith200855-61"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Shoghi Effendi throughout his lifetime translated <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_texts" title="Bahá'í texts" class="mw-redirect">Bahá'í texts</a>; developed global plans for the expansion of the Bahá'í community; developed the <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_World_Centre" title="Bahá'í World Centre">Bahá'í World Centre</a>; carried on a voluminous correspondence with communities and individuals around the world; and built the administrative structure of the religion, preparing the community for the election of the Universal House of Justice.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHutter2005737.E2.80.93740_3-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHutter2005737.E2.80.93740-3"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> He died in 1957 under conditions that did not allow for a successor to be appointed.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETaherzadeh2000347-363_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETaherzadeh2000347-363-62"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith200858.E2.80.9369_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith200858.E2.80.9369-63"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>At local, regional, and national levels, Bahá'ís elect members to nine-person <a href="/wiki/Spiritual_Assembly" title="Spiritual Assembly">Spiritual Assemblies</a>, which run the affairs of the religion. There are also <a href="/wiki/Institution_of_the_Counsellors" title="Institution of the Counsellors">appointed individuals</a> working at various levels, including locally and internationally, which perform the function of propagating the teachings and protecting the community. The latter do not serve as clergy, which the Bahá'í Faith does not have.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDaumeWatson1992_24-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDaumeWatson1992-24"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2008160_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2008160-64"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> The Universal House of Justice, first elected in 1963, remains the successor and supreme governing body of the Bahá'í Faith, and its 9 members are elected every five years by the members of all National Spiritual Assemblies.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStockman1995_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStockman1995-65"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> Any male Bahá'í, 21 years or older, is eligible to be elected to the Universal House of Justice; all other positions are open to male and female Bahá'ís.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2008205_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2008205-66"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_plans">International plans</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: International plans">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Willmette_how.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A white domed building with a large garden leading toward it" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Willmette_how.jpg/220px-Willmette_how.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Willmette_how.jpg/330px-Willmette_how.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Willmette_how.jpg/440px-Willmette_how.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="750" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Willmette_how.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_House_of_Worship_(Wilmette,_Illinois)" title="Bahá'í House of Worship (Wilmette, Illinois)">Bahá'í House of Worship</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wilmette,_Illinois" title="Wilmette, Illinois">Wilmette, Illinois</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1937, Shoghi Effendi launched a seven-year plan for the Bahá'ís of North America, followed by another in 1946.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDaneshDaneshDanesh1991_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDaneshDaneshDanesh1991-67"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1953, he launched the first international plan, the <a href="/wiki/Ten_Year_Crusade" title="Ten Year Crusade">Ten Year World Crusade</a>. This plan included extremely ambitious goals for the expansion of Bahá'í communities and institutions, the translation of <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_texts" title="Bahá'í texts" class="mw-redirect">Bahá'í texts</a> into several new languages, and the sending of <a href="/wiki/Pioneering_(Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD)" title="Pioneering (Bahá'í)">Bahá'í pioneers</a> into previously unreached nations.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHassal19961-21_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHassal19961-21-68"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> He announced in letters during the Ten Year Crusade that it would be followed by other plans under the direction of the Universal House of Justice, which was elected in 1963 at the culmination of the Crusade. The House of Justice then launched a nine-year plan in 1964, and a series of subsequent multi-year plans of varying length and goals followed, guiding the direction of the international Bahá'í community.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmithMomen198963-91_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmithMomen198963-91-69"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Annually, on 21 April, the Universal House of Justice sends a ‘<a href="/wiki/Ridv%C3%A1n" title="Ridván">Ridván</a>’ message to the worldwide Bahá’í community,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2000297_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2000297-70"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> which generally gives an update on the progress made concerning the current plan, and provides further guidance for the year to come.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>note 6<span>]</span></a></sup> The Bahá'ís around the world are currently being encouraged to focus on capacity building through children's classes, youth groups, devotional gatherings, and a systematic study of the religion known as <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_study_circle" title="Bahá'í study circle">study circles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGervais2008_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGervais2008-72"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUniversal_House_of_Justice17_January_2003_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUniversal_House_of_Justice17_January_2003-73"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> Further focuses are involvement in social action and participation in the prevalent discourses of society.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVahedi2_March_2011_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVahedi2_March_2011-74"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUniversal_House_of_Justice21_April_2010_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUniversal_House_of_Justice21_April_2010-75"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> The years from 2001 until 2021 represent four successive five-year plans, culminating in the centennial anniversary of the passing of <a href="/wiki/%60Abdu%27l-Bah%C3%A1" title="`Abdu'l-Bahá">`Abdu'l-Bahá</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUniversal_House_Of_Justice2006_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUniversal_House_Of_Justice2006-76"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith_by_country" title="Bahá'í Faith by country" class="mw-redirect">Bahá'í Faith by country</a></div>
<div class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_statistics" title="Bahá'í statistics">Bahá'í statistics</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a href="/wiki/File:New_delhi_temple.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A large temple in the shape of an open lotus flower" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/New_delhi_temple.jpg/280px-New_delhi_temple.jpg" width="280" height="186" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/New_delhi_temple.jpg/420px-New_delhi_temple.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/New_delhi_temple.jpg/560px-New_delhi_temple.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1063" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:New_delhi_temple.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Lotus_Temple" title="Lotus Temple">Lotus Temple</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_House_of_Worship" title="Bahá'í House of Worship">Bahá'í House of Worship</a> in New Delhi, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>. It attracts an average of 4 million visitors a year.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A Bahá'í published document reported 4.74 million Bahá'ís in 1986 growing at a rate of 4.4%.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERabbaniJuly_19872-7_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERabbaniJuly_19872-7-77"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> Bahá'í sources since 1991 usually estimate the worldwide Bahá'í population to be above 5 million.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBah.C3.A1.27.C3.AD_World_News_Service2010_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBah.C3.A1.27.C3.AD_World_News_Service2010-78"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> The <i>World Christian Encyclopedia</i> estimated 7.1 million Bahá'ís in the world in 2000, representing 218 countries,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarrett20014_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarrett20014-79"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> and 7.3 million in 2010<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAssociation_of_Religion_Data_Archives2010_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAssociation_of_Religion_Data_Archives2010-80"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> with the same source. They further state: "The Baha'i Faith is the only religion to have grown faster in every United Nations region over the past 100 years than the general population; Baha’i was thus the fastest-growing religion between 1910 and 2010, growing at least twice as fast as the population of almost every UN region."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJohnsonGrim26_March_201359-62_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJohnsonGrim26_March_201359-62-81"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> This source's only systematic flaw was to consistently have a higher estimate of Christians than other cross-national data sets.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHsuReynoldsHackettGibbon2008691.E2.80.93692_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHsuReynoldsHackettGibbon2008691.E2.80.93692-82"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>From its origins in the <a href="/wiki/Qajar_dynasty" title="Qajar dynasty">Persian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman</a> Empires, by the early 20th century there were a number of converts in <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_East_Asia" title="South East Asia" class="mw-redirect">South East Asia</a>, Europe, and North America. During the 1950s and 1960s, vast <a href="/wiki/Pioneering_(Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD)" title="Pioneering (Bahá'í)">travel teaching</a> efforts brought the religion to almost every country and territory of the world. By the 1990s, Bahá'ís were developing programs for systematic consolidation on a large scale, and the early 21st century saw large influxes of new adherents around the world. The Bahá'í Faith is currently the largest religious minority in Iran,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEInternational_Federation_of_Human_RightsAugust_2003_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEInternational_Federation_of_Human_RightsAugust_2003-83"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> Panama,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAssociation_of_Religion_Data_Archives2010.5Bhttp:.2F.2Fwww.thearda.com.2FinternationalData.2Fcountries.2FCountry_174_2.asp_National_Profile:_Panama.5D_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAssociation_of_Religion_Data_Archives2010.5Bhttp:.2F.2Fwww.thearda.com.2FinternationalData.2Fcountries.2FCountry_174_2.asp_National_Profile:_Panama.5D-84"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> and Belize;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAssociation_of_Religion_Data_Archives2010.5Bhttp:.2F.2Fwww.thearda.com.2FinternationalData.2Fcountries.2FCountry_23_2.asp_National_Profile:_Belize.5D_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAssociation_of_Religion_Data_Archives2010.5Bhttp:.2F.2Fwww.thearda.com.2FinternationalData.2Fcountries.2FCountry_23_2.asp_National_Profile:_Belize.5D-85"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> the second largest international religion in Bolivia,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAssociation_of_Religion_Data_Archives2010.5Bhttp:.2F.2Fwww.thearda.com.2FinternationalData.2Fcountries.2FCountry_27_2.asp_National_Profile:_Bolivia.5D_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAssociation_of_Religion_Data_Archives2010.5Bhttp:.2F.2Fwww.thearda.com.2FinternationalData.2Fcountries.2FCountry_27_2.asp_National_Profile:_Bolivia.5D-86"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> Zambia,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAssociation_of_Religion_Data_Archives2010.5Bhttp:.2F.2Fwww.thearda.com.2FinternationalData.2Fcountries.2FCountry_245_2.asp_National_Profile:_Zambia.5D_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAssociation_of_Religion_Data_Archives2010.5Bhttp:.2F.2Fwww.thearda.com.2FinternationalData.2Fcountries.2FCountry_245_2.asp_National_Profile:_Zambia.5D-87"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> and Papua New Guinea;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAssociation_of_Religion_Data_Archives2010.5Bhttp:.2F.2Fwww.thearda.com.2FinternationalData.2Fcountries.2FCountry_175_2.asp_National_Profile:_Papua_New_Guinea.5D_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAssociation_of_Religion_Data_Archives2010.5Bhttp:.2F.2Fwww.thearda.com.2FinternationalData.2Fcountries.2FCountry_175_2.asp_National_Profile:_Papua_New_Guinea.5D-88"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> and the third largest international religion in Chad<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReligious_Intelligence_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReligious_Intelligence-89"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAssociation_of_Religion_Data_Archives2010.5Bhttp:.2F.2Fwww.thearda.com.2FinternationalData.2Fcountries.2FCountry_45_2.asp_National_Profile:_Chad.5D_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAssociation_of_Religion_Data_Archives2010.5Bhttp:.2F.2Fwww.thearda.com.2FinternationalData.2Fcountries.2FCountry_45_2.asp_National_Profile:_Chad.5D-90"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> and Kenya.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAssociation_of_Religion_Data_Archives2010.5Bhttp:.2F.2Fwww.thearda.com.2FinternationalData.2Fcountries.2FCountry_121_2.asp_National_Profiles:_Kenya.5D_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAssociation_of_Religion_Data_Archives2010.5Bhttp:.2F.2Fwww.thearda.com.2FinternationalData.2Fcountries.2FCountry_121_2.asp_National_Profiles:_Kenya.5D-91"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>According to <i><a href="/wiki/World_Almanac" title="World Almanac">The World Almanac and Book of Facts 2004</a></i>:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>The majority of Bahá'ís live in Asia (3.6 million), Africa (1.8 million), and Latin America (900,000). According to some estimates, the largest Bahá'í community in the world is in <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, with 2.2 million Bahá'ís, next is <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>, with 350,000, the US, with 150,000, and Brazil, with 60,000. Aside from these countries, numbers vary greatly. Currently, no country has a Bahá'í majority.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPark2004_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPark2004-92"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>The Bahá'í religion was listed in <i>The Britannica Book of the Year</i> (1992–present) as the second most widespread of the world's independent religions in terms of the number of countries represented. According to <i>Britannica</i>, the Bahá'í Faith (as of 2002) is established in 247 countries and territories; represents over 2,100 ethnic, racial, and tribal groups; has scriptures translated into over 800 languages; and has an estimated seven million adherents worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEncyclop.C3.A6dia_Britannica2002_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEncyclop.C3.A6dia_Britannica2002-93"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> Additionally, Bahá'ís have <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_administration" title="Bahá'í administration">self-organized</a> in most of the nations of the world.</p>
<p>The Bahá'í religion was ranked by the Foreign Policy magazine as the world's second <a href="/wiki/Fastest_growing_religion" title="Fastest growing religion" class="mw-redirect">fastest growing religion</a> by percentage (1.7%) in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEForeign_Policy_Magazine1_May_2007_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEForeign_Policy_Magazine1_May_2007-94"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_practices">Social practices</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Social practices">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Laws">Laws</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Laws">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_laws" title="Bahá'í laws">Bahá'í laws</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_gardens_by_David_Shankbone.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Elaborate gardens with several gates and a walkway leading to a domed building in the distance" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_gardens_by_David_Shankbone.jpg/220px-Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_gardens_by_David_Shankbone.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_gardens_by_David_Shankbone.jpg/330px-Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_gardens_by_David_Shankbone.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_gardens_by_David_Shankbone.jpg/440px-Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_gardens_by_David_Shankbone.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_gardens_by_David_Shankbone.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_gardens" title="Bahá'í gardens">Bahá'í gardens</a> in <a href="/wiki/Haifa,_Israel" title="Haifa, Israel" class="mw-redirect">Haifa, Israel</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The laws of the Bahá'í Faith primarily come from the <i><a href="/wiki/Kit%C3%A1b-i-Aqdas" title="Kitáb-i-Aqdas">Kitáb-i-Aqdas</a></i>, written by Bahá'u'lláh.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2000223-225_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2000223-225-95"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> The following are a few examples of basic laws and religious observances.</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Prayer_in_the_Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith" title="Prayer in the Bahá'í Faith">Prayer in the Bahá'í Faith</a> consists of obligatory prayer and devotional (general) prayer. Bahá'ís over the age of 15 must individually recite an <a href="/wiki/Obligatory_Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_prayers" title="Obligatory Bahá'í prayers">obligatory prayer</a> each day, using fixed words and form. In addition to the daily obligatory prayer, believers are directed to daily offer <a href="/wiki/Prayer_in_the_Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith" title="Prayer in the Bahá'í Faith">devotional prayer</a> and to meditate and study sacred scripture. There is no set form for devotions and meditations, though the devotional prayers written by the central figures of the Bahá'í Faith and collected in prayer books are held in high esteem. Reading aloud of prayers from prayer books is a typical feature of Bahá'í gatherings.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Backbiting" title="Backbiting">Backbiting</a> and gossip are prohibited and denounced.</li>
<li>Adult Bahá'ís in good health should observe a <a href="/wiki/Nineteen_Day_Fast" title="Nineteen Day Fast">nineteen-day sunrise-to-sunset fast</a> each year from 2 March through 20 March.</li>
<li>Bahá'ís are forbidden to drink <a href="/wiki/Alcoholic_beverage" title="Alcoholic beverage">alcohol</a> or to take drugs, unless prescribed by doctors.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sexual_intercourse" title="Sexual intercourse">Sexual intercourse</a> is only permitted between a husband and wife, and thus <a href="/wiki/Premarital" title="Premarital" class="mw-redirect">premarital</a>, <a href="/wiki/Extramarital_sex" title="Extramarital sex">extramarital</a>, and homosexual intercourse are forbidden. <i>(See also <a href="/wiki/Homosexuality_and_the_Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith" title="Homosexuality and the Bahá'í Faith">Homosexuality and the Bahá'í Faith</a>)</i></li>
<li>Gambling is forbidden.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fanaticism" title="Fanaticism">Fanaticism</a> is forbidden.</li>
<li>Adherence to <a href="/wiki/Ritual" title="Ritual">ritual</a> is discouraged, with the notable exception of the obligatory prayers.</li>
<li>Abstaining from <a href="/wiki/Partisan_(political)" title="Partisan (political)">partisan</a> politics is required.</li>
</ul>
<p>While some of the laws from the Kitáb-i-Aqdas are applicable at the present time and may be enforced to a degree by the administrative institutions,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2008158.E2.80.93161_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2008158.E2.80.93161-96"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> Bahá'u'lláh has provided for the progressive application of other laws that are dependent upon the existence of a predominantly Bahá'í society. The laws, when not in direct conflict with the civil laws of the country of residence, are binding on every Bahá'í,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2008158_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2008158-97"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> and the observance of personal laws, such as <a href="/wiki/Prayer_in_the_Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith" title="Prayer in the Bahá'í Faith">prayer</a> or fasting, is the sole responsibility of the individual.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2000223-225_95-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2000223-225-95"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWalbridge1996_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWalbridge1996-98"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marriage">Marriage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Marriage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_marriage" title="Bahá'í marriage">Bahá'í marriage</a></div>
